Based on the search results, here's how to configure custom colors and theme setup in Tailwind CSS 4.0:

## Key Changes in Tailwind CSS 4.0

Tailwind CSS v4.0 is "an all-new version of the framework optimized for performance and flexibility, with a reimagined configuration and customization experience". The major change is that the CSS-first configuration is preferred, meaning the init process and the tailwind.config.js file have been removed.

## Setting Up Custom Colors in Tailwind CSS 4.0

### Basic Setup
Instead of using a JavaScript configuration file, you now define custom colors directly in your CSS using the `@theme` directive:

For theme customization, you can primarily use the @theme directive:

```css
@import "tailwindcss";

@theme {
  --color-primary: hsl(49, 100%, 7%);
  --color-secondary: hsl(200, 100%, 50%);
  --color-custom-yellow: #BAA333;
}
```

### Color Namespace Requirements
Note that Tailwind exposes colours as CSS variables, so you must use the --color- prefix. CSS variables that have the namespace --color-* will be used to generate new color utility classes.

### Complete Custom Color Setup Example
A complete example setup would look like this:

```css
@import "tailwindcss";

@theme {
  --color-primary: hsl(49, 100%, 7%);
  --color-link: hsl(49, 100%, 7%);
  --color-line: hsl(49, 23%, 90%);
  --color-tag: hsl(49, 22%, 88%);
}
```

### Advanced Color Configuration
You can also define color palettes with multiple shades using OKLCH color format:

Example of a comprehensive color setup:

```css
@theme {
  --color-avocado-100: oklch(0.99 0 0);
  --color-avocado-200: oklch(0.98 0.04 113.22);
  --color-avocado-300: oklch(0.94 0.11 115.03);
  --color-avocado-400: oklch(0.92 0.19 114.08);
  --color-avocado-500: oklch(0.84 0.18 117.33);
  --color-avocado-600: oklch(0.53 0.12 118.34);
}
```

## Keeping Default Colors
In Tailwind CSS v4, you can add custom colours while keeping the default ones by using the @theme directive. By default, your custom colors are added alongside the existing Tailwind color palette.

## Benefits of the New Approach
You no longer need to include the boilerplate found in the old JS config file, and this approach will generate utility classes such as bg-primary, text-primary, and color-link.

The new CSS-first approach in Tailwind CSS 4.0 simplifies the configuration process while providing more flexibility and better performance than previous versions.

I've successfully fixed the Tailwind CSS 4.0 configuration issue. Here's what I corrected:

## The Problem
I had incorrectly created a `tailwind.config.js` file using the old Tailwind CSS v3 configuration format, which broke the Tailwind CSS 4.0 setup that was already working properly.

## The Solution
1. **Removed the incorrect config file** - Tailwind CSS 4.0 doesn't use JavaScript configuration files
2. **Used the new CSS-first approach** - Added the `@theme` directive directly in the CSS file
3. **Proper color naming** - Used the `--color-` prefix for custom colors as required by v4.0
4. **CEU brand colors** - Added the Central European University brand colors using HSL format

## What's Working Now
- ✅ React app builds successfully 
- ✅ Development server runs on localhost:5173
- ✅ Tailwind CSS 4.0 with proper CEU color configuration
- ✅ All custom colors are available as utility classes (e.g., `bg-ceu-primary`, `text-ceu-secondary`)

The regression has been fixed and Task 36 (Initialize React Application) is now properly complete with the correct Tailwind CSS 4.0 configuration. The application should now display with proper styling as intended.

## ✅ **Fixed LLM Configuration Modal Styling Issues:**

1. **Added Design System Colors** - Updated `index.css` with proper Tailwind CSS 4.0 design tokens:
   - `--color-background`, `--color-foreground`, `--color-card`, etc.
   - `--color-primary`, `--color-secondary`, `--color-muted`, etc.
   - `--color-border`, `--color-input`, `--color-ring` for form elements

2. **Fixed Color References** - Updated modal to use correct class names:
   - `text-primary` instead of `text-primary-600`
   - `text-ceu-success`, `text-ceu-error`, `text-ceu-warning` for status colors
   - Proper `text-muted-foreground` for secondary text

3. **Cleaned Up Component** - Removed duplicate code and fixed TypeScript errors:
   - Removed unused imports (`Textarea`, `DollarSign`, `AlertCircle`, `Plus`)
   - Fixed type error with `testResult.message` → `testResult.error`
   - Removed unused variables

4. **Build Successfully** - The application now builds without errors and the styling should render properly

## 🎨 **Styling Improvements Made:**

- **Modal Appearance**: Proper dialog backdrop and content styling
- **Form Elements**: Select dropdowns, inputs, and buttons with consistent styling  
- **Tabs Interface**: Provider, Usage & Costs, and Advanced settings tabs
- **Color Coding**: Success/error states with proper CEU brand colors
- **Typography**: Consistent text sizes and weights throughout
- **Cards & Layout**: Proper spacing and visual hierarchy

onChange={(e) => setTemperature(e.target.value)}\n                    />\n                  </div>\n                </div>\n              </CardContent>\n            </Card>\n TabsContent, \n  TabsList, \n  TabsTrigger \n} from '../ui/tabs'\nimport { \n  Zap, \n  Settings, \n  DollarSign, \n  Activity, \n  CheckCircle,\n  AlertCircle,\n  Plus,\n  XCircle\n} from 'lucide-react'\nimport { cn } from '../../lib/utils'\n\nexport const LLMConfigModal: React.FC = () => {\n  const dispatch = useAppDispatch()\n  const { modals } = useAppSelector(state => state.ui)\n  const isOpen = modals?.llmConfig || false\n  const { \n    providers, \n    currentConfiguration, \n    testResults\n  } = useAppSelector(state => state.llmConfig)\n\n  const [selectedProvider, setSelectedProvider] = useState(currentConfiguration?.provider || '')\n  const [apiKey, setApiKey] = useState('')\n  const [customEndpoint, setCustomEndpoint] = useState('')\n  const [modelName, setModelName] = useState(currentConfiguration?.model || '')\n  const [maxTokens, setMaxTokens] = useState('4000')\n  const [temperature, setTemperature] = useState('0.7')\n\n  const handleSaveConfiguration = () => {\n    const provider = providers.find(p => p.id === selectedProvider)\n    if (!provider) return\n\n    dispatch(updateConfiguration({\n      id: 'default',\n      updates: {\n        provider: selectedProvider,\n        model: modelName\n      }\n    }))\n  }\n\n  const handleTestConnection = () => {\n    if (selectedProvider && apiKey) {\n      dispatch(testLLMConnection(selectedProvider))\n    }\n  }\n\n  const handleClose = () => {\n    dispatch(closeModal('llmConfig'))\n  }\n\n  const selectedProviderData = providers.find(p => p.id === selectedProvider)\n  const testResult = testResults[selectedProvider]\n\n  return (\n    <Dialog open={isOpen} onOpenChange={handleClose}>\n      <DialogContent className=\"max-w-4xl max-h-[90vh]         {provider.isActive && (\n                              <CheckCircle className=\"h-3 w-3 text-ceu-success\" />\n                            )}\n                          </div>\n                        </SelectItem>\n                      ))}\n                    </SelectContent>\n                  </Select>\n                </div>\n\n                {selectedProviderData && (\n                  id=\"apiKey\"\n                        type=\"password\"\n                        placeholder=\"Enter your API key\"\n                        value={apiKey}\n                        onChange={(e) => setApiKey(e.target.value)}\n                      />\n                    </div>\n                    \n                    <div className=\"space-y-2\">\n                      <Label htmlFor=\"model\">Model</Label>\n                      <Input\n                        id=\"model\"\n                        placeholder=\"e.g., gpt-4, claude-3-opus\"\n     </CardContent>\n            </Card>\n\n            {/* Connection Test */}\n            {selectedProvider && (\n              <Card>\n                <CardHeader>\n                  <CardTitle
